ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-item {
    counter-increment: list-counter-alpha;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-alpha, lower-alpha);
}

/* Level 3: Lowercase roman numerals */

    counter-reset: list-counter-roman;
}

    counter-increment: list-counter-roman;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-roman, lower-roman);
}

data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT FOUR: CONTRACEPTIVE TECHNOLOGY</p>
<p>In this unit you will study the principles of contraceptive technology and will cover all methods of family planning, both natural and modern.</p>
<p>This unit is composed of four sections:
Section One: Current Contraceptive Principles
Section Two: Natural Family Planning and Lactation
Amenorrhoea
Section Three: Hormonal Contraceptives
Section Four: Other Contraceptive Methods</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-objectives">Unit Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>List the principles used in current contraceptive technology</li>
<li>Explain the physiology of natural family planning and lactation amenorrhoea</li>
<li>Describe the different types of hormonal contraceptives</li>
<li>Describe non-hormonal types of contraceptives, which include IUCDs, VSC and barrier methods</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-1-current-contraceptive-principles">SECTION 1: CURRENT CONTRACEPTIVE PRINCIPLES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-1-current-contraceptive-principles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this section you are going to be introduced to the principles currently used in contraceptive technology. You will occasionally be referred to module one, and the section on counselling and infection prevention. You will also review module two unit one section one, which discusses the policy guidelines and standards on Reproductive Health (RH), and section four, which deals with safe motherhood.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define family planning (FP)</li>
<li>List the benefits of family planning</li>
<li>State the guidelines and standards of family planning/reproductive health</li>
<li>Explain counselling in relation to family planning</li>
<li>State the patient assessment prior to family planning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="family-planning">Family Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-is-family-planning">What is Family Planning?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-do-you-think-family-planning-is-did-you-think-of-this">What do you think family planning is? Did you think of this?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-do-you-think-family-planning-is-did-you-think-of-this" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Family planning is the process of child spacing so that the couple has the number of children they want at the time desired, that is, when wanted, expected and welcomed.</p>
<p>Refer to unit one for further details and clarification.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="benefits-of-family-planning">Benefits of Family Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benefits-of-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Family planning enables couples and individuals to decide freely and responsibly on the number and spacing of their children, as well as on the most appropriate time of having them.</p>
<p>Family planning helps everyone. The health benefits of FP play a major role in protecting and promoting the quality of lives, not only of the infants but of their siblings and the family as a whole.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="can-you-think-of-three-benefits-of-family-planning">Can you think of three benefits of family planning?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#can-you-think-of-three-benefits-of-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There are several benefits of family planning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="medical-benefits">Medical Benefits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-benefits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Medical benefits differ depending on the target population. Some of the benefits of family planning for women are shown below.</p>
<ul>
<li>Their health is better as they are protected against unwanted pregnancy, hence death related to high risk pregnancy and abortion is reduced.</li>
<li>Some methods, such as the hormonal method, have additional (non-contraceptive) benefits, including the reduction of anaemia and cancer of the genital tract.</li>
<li>Barrier methods minimise the transmission of STIs and HIV/AIDS if used properly.</li>
<li>Mothers become healthier as they avoid the extremes of maternal age and carry their pregnancies within the optimal child bearing age bracket of 19 to 35 years, before and after which the mothers are at high risk of developing complications related to pregnancy.</li>
<li>There is a decrease in the risks of abortion as the baby is welcome and the</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 213 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>mother well prepared physically and psychologically for the pregnancy.</p>
<ul>
<li>There are reduced fertility and mortality rates.</li>
<li>There are improved health facilities and death related to pregnancy and childbirth is reduced.</li>
</ul>
<p>There are also medical advantages to the children.</p>
<ul>
<li>Children are healthier, since the optimum spacing between births is 27 to 38 months, giving the mother the time to nurse and care for the infant.</li>
<li>The death related to infections and malnutrition to the under fives is reduced.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="social-benefits">Social Benefits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#social-benefits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The social benefits related to family planning are numerous.</p>
<ul>
<li>There is an improved relationship with the spouse and family due to less stress and better social life.</li>
<li>Socially healthy families are productive and economically more stable as they participate in community development and nation building.</li>
<li>Women learn to make informed choices.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="national-benefits">National Benefits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#national-benefits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are several benefits associated with family planning on a national level.</p>
<ul>
<li>The country is able to budget for its citizens as the birth rate will be controlled.</li>
<li>Nationally reduced fertility and mortality rates lessen the burden to the nation.</li>
</ul>
<p>You should note that countries with high fertility rates have poor health conditions in general, and inadequate health facilities substantially increase the risk of pregnancy related deaths. (Hatcher: July 1997)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="scope-of-family-planning">Scope of Family Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scope-of-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You will now cover the steps that help the health provider in the provision of FP.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="counselling">Counselling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#counselling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Family planning service providers should be competent in counselling on topics related to all FP methods.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="provision-of-contraceptives">Provision of Contraceptives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#provision-of-contraceptives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should provide contraceptives to patients in accordance with the suitable method chosen by the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="follow-up-and-referral-system">Follow Up and Referral System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#follow-up-and-referral-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All patients who choose a method of FP should be informed of the appropriate follow up requirements and encouraged to return to the clinic in case of any concerns. Providers should use the established referral system for appropriate management of identified conditions that need further attention.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="record-keeping">Record Keeping<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#record-keeping" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The service provider should keep proper records of each patient. Keep up to date records on contraceptive distribution as well. All service delivery points (SDPs), NGOs and other stakeholders should follow the Ministry of Health Guidelines on Service Provision and Record Keeping. This helps in compiling statistical data for health care planning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="supervision">Supervision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Supervision is an essential component of program evaluation. It ensures that the guidelines are being followed and patient needs are being met. It helps in the assessment of the quality of care given and whether the patient's rights are being observed. Furthermore, it motivates service providers as they can express and discuss views with their superiors. Continued supervision will enable you to pinpoint areas for improvement.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="logistics">Logistics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#logistics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main objective of logistics management is to deliver the right product in the right quantity, in the right condition, to the right place, at the right time for the right cost.</p>
<p>Proper maintenance of a logistics system helps the providers to avoid both understocking and overstocking in order to maintain quality. The service provider must ensure proper storage and handling of contraceptive commodities for the stipulated shelf life. The contraceptives are removed from the shelf systematically (that is, first in first out) thereby ensuring those nearing expiry are used first.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="logistics">Logistics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#logistics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main objective of logistics management is to deliver the right product in the right quantity, in</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>the right condition, to the right place, at the right time for the right cost.</p>
<p>Proper maintenance of a logistics system helps the providers to avoid both understocking and overstocking in order to maintain quality. The service provider must ensure proper storage and handling of contraceptive commodities for the stipulated shelf life. The contraceptives are removed from the shelf systematically (that is, first in first out) thereby ensuring those nearing expiry are used first.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="counselling-in-family-planning">Counselling in Family Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#counselling-in-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="do-you-remember-the-definition-of-counselling-as-covered-in-module-one">Do you remember the definition of counselling as covered in module one?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#do-you-remember-the-definition-of-counselling-as-covered-in-module-one" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Counselling is the act of working with a patient to help them clarify personal goals and find ways of overcoming their problems with the aim of assisting the individual to change behaviours that are interfering with attainment of basic needs.</p>
<p>For the purpose of FP, counselling is viewed as the</p>
<p>art whereby the service provider guides/assists a</p>
<p>patient to make an informed choice in matters regarding their RH needs, taking into account all the surrounding circumstances and the patient's personal needs at the time.</p>
<p>Counselling is a vital part of RH care. It helps patients to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Arrive at an informed choice of RH options</li>
<li>Select a contraceptive method with which they are satisfied</li>
<li>Use the chosen method safely and effectively</li>
</ul>
<p>Counselling in family planning is an important tool when serving patients. It is important to remember that they have:</p>
<ul>
<li>The right to decide whether or not to practise FP</li>
<li>The freedom to choose which method to use</li>
<li>The right of privacy and confidentiality</li>
<li>The right to refuse any type of examination</li>
</ul>
<p>While many contraceptive methods are highly effective, method failure can occur. In case of method failure, the patient should be counselled, informed about available options and referred for appropriate services.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-in-counselling-a-patient-for-family-planning">Steps in Counselling a Patient for Family Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-in-counselling-a-patient-for-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are six steps used in counselling a family planning patient.</p>
<p>Can you remember what they are?</p>
<ul>
<li>Greet, welcome and make the client feel comfortable. Establish a good rapport.</li>
<li>Ask the patient about themselves and any FP experiences. Get all the information about the patient.</li>
<li>Tell patient of the available methods and reproductive choices.</li>
<li>Help the patient make informed choices through history taking, general examination and finding out the real needs. Avoid biases.</li>
<li>Explain in detail the method of choice and give detailed instructions on how to use the method.</li>
<li>Return visits explained and discussion encouraged.</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>G</th><th>Greet, welcome and make the patient feel comfortable. Establish a good rapport.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>A</td><td>Ask the patient about themselves and any FP experiences. Get all the information about the patient.</td></tr><tr><td>T</td><td>Tell the patient of the available methods and reproductive choices.</td></tr><tr><td>H</td><td>Help the patient make informed choices through history taking, general examination and finding out the real needs. Avoid biases.</td></tr><tr><td>E</td><td>Explain in detail the method of choice and give detailed instructions on how to use the method.</td></tr><tr><td>R</td><td>Return visits explained and discussion encouraged.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-counselling-process">The Counselling Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-counselling-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As a service provider, you need to review all available contraceptive methods that your patient may choose from. As a counsellor, you should be aware of a number of factors about each patient that may be important, depending on the method to be used. These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>The reproductive goal of the woman or couple (spacing or timing of births)</li>
<li>Personal factors including the time, travel costs, pain or discomfort likely to be experienced</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Accessibility and availability of other products that are necessary to use the method</li>
<li>The need for protection against STIs and HIV/AIDS</li>
</ul>
<p>There are three phases of counselling.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="initial-counselling">Initial Counselling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#initial-counselling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Initial counselling is carried out at reception, where</p>
<p>you have to describe all the methods available and</p>
<p>help the patient to choose the method appropriate</p>
<p>for themselves.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method-specific-counselling">Method Specific Counselling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method-specific-counselling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Method specific counselling is carried out prior to</p>
<p>and immediately following service provision. Here,</p>
<p>you need to give instructions to the patient on how</p>
<p>to use the method chosen. You should also discuss</p>
<p>possible common side effects specific to the method</p>
<p>and explain what should be done if that happens.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="follow-up-counseling">Follow up counseling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#follow-up-counseling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Follow up counselling occurs during the return visit.</p>
<p>Ask the patient about method use, satisfaction and</p>
<p>any problems that may have occurred.</p>
<p>Do you know who should provide counselling?</p>
<p>All the staff should be knowledgeable about all available contraceptive methods so as to be in a position to give information and counsel effectively. (MOH: March 2005).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="patient-assessment">Patient Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patient-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The patient assessment will help you to give an appropriate method of contraception to an individual patient. In many ways counselling forms a part of patient assessment since both go together as you assist the patient to make an informed choice about the most appropriate method.</p>
<p>The main objective of carrying out a patient assessment is to determine:</p>
<ul>
<li>That the patient is not pregnant</li>
<li>Whether any conditions requiring additional care for a particular method exist</li>
<li>Whether there are any special problems that require further assessment, treatment or regular follow up or referral</li>
<li>Whether there are need for HIV/AIDs services and, if so, to provide the services or arrange the appropriate referral</li>
</ul>
<p>To achieve the above objective, you have to be careful with the questions you ask and remain attentive to the patient's concerns. Furthermore, you need to clarify any points that you feel the patient does not understand clearly.</p>
<p>How can you be reasonably sure that a female patient is not pregnant?</p>
<p>You can only be reasonably sure a patient is not pregnant when she has no signs and symptoms of pregnancy and exhibits the following characteristics:</p>
<ul>
<li>Has had no intercourse since her last menses</li>
<li>Is within seven days after the start of her menses (days one to seven)</li>
<li>Is within four weeks postpartum (for non-breast feeding women)</li>
<li>Is within seven days post abortion</li>
<li>Is fully breast feeding less than six months post partum and has had no menstrual bleeding</li>
<li>Has been correctly and consistently using another reliable contraceptive method</li>
</ul>
<p>Pelvic examination is seldom necessary except to rule out pregnancy of more than six weeks, measured from the Last Menstrual Period (LMP).</p>
<p>A pregnancy test is not essential, except in cases where:</p>
<ul>
<li>It is difficult to confirm pregnancy (that is, six weeks or less after the LMP)</li>
<li>The results of pelvic examination are unequivocal (for example, with an overweight patient sizing the uterus may be difficult)</li>
</ul>
<p>If pregnancy testing is not available, counsel the patient to use a barrier method or abstain from</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers
Page 216 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>intercourse until her menses occur or pregnancy is confirmed.</p>
<p>Remember:</p>
<ol>
<li>No contraceptive method with the exception of condoms (and the diaphragm to a lesser degree), provides protection against Genital Tract Infections (GTIs) and other STIs such as Hepatitis B or HIV/AIDS.</li>
<li>During the counselling sessions, explain to all patients the risks of GTI and STI transmission.</li>
</ol>
<p>Most contraceptive methods can be provided after asking a few key questions. However, Intra Uterine Contraceptive Devices (IUCDs) and Voluntary Surgical Contraceptives (VSCs) do require a physical and pelvic examination to be performed before use. This brings us to the examinations that you may have to perform routinely and annually on your patients.</p>
<p>Below are the special procedures a patient may go through to enhance her good reproductive health. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>General physical examination</li>
<li>Breast examination</li>
<li>Pelvic examination</li>
<li>Papanicolau smear</li>
</ul>
<p>General Physical Examination</p>
<p>What do you think is the purpose of a physical examination?</p>
<p>The main purpose of a physical examination is:</p>
<ul>
<li>To assess the general health status of a patient</li>
<li>To aid in making a diagnosis</li>
</ul>
<p>A physical examination should be performed either as part of a routine medical examination or in case of sickness. You are expected to carry out a systematic head to toe examination, noting:</p>
<ul>
<li>Health status</li>
<li>Nutritional status</li>
<li>Behaviour</li>
<li>Mental state</li>
<li>Speech</li>
<li>Ability to walk</li>
</ul>
<p>You should also check for signs of anaemia, infection, jaundice, hypertension and deep venous thrombosis. (NCK:1988; MOH:1988)</p>
<p>Breast Examination</p>
<p>This is a very important examination for a family planner.</p>
<p>See if you can answer the questions below.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-a7288170.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<p>The entire surface of the breast including the tail is palpated in a clockwise fashion.</p>
<p>Why should you perform a breast examination?</p>
<p>The main reason for performing a breast examination is to enable you to detect abnormalities (such as cancer of the breast) and take appropriate action.</p>
<p>When should a breast examination be performed?</p>
<p>From the age of 20 years all females should do Self Breast Examination (SBE) immediately after their menstrual period. If the patient is on the pill, she should perform her SBE on the day she starts a new packet. Those in menopause should do a SBE on the first day of each calendar month.</p>
<p>How do you perform a breast examination?</p>
<p>This is the method whereby the patient inspects, palpates and expresses both breasts. The axilla is also palpated for any nodules.</p>
<p>Inspection</p>
<p>Ask the patient to undress and sit or stand relaxed in front of a mirror with good lighting. With hands at the sides, on the waist and on the head respectively, check on the size, shape, discoloration and retraction (dimpling) of the nipple. Turn from side to side and look underneath, push the hands inward and</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>outwards until the chest muscles tighten. Check again at the breasts while pressing and note any puckering of the skin or retraction of the nipple.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-3f92b4c3.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="palpation">Palpation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#palpation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ask the patient to lie down in a dorsal position on a firm surface with her head on a pillow. Tell her to put her left hand on top of the head folded and then use the right hand to examine the left breast. She should then reverse this to examine the right breast. Emphasise that she should examine one breast at a time using the flat of her fingers but not the fingertips. The fingers should be kept flat and close together. Instruct her how to divide the breast into quadrants (four areas), and starting with the upper scale near the collarbone, to press gently but firmly towards the body and going round the whole breast clockwise to check for any lumps. Show her how to examine the tail of the breast by going right up into the hollow of the armpit. Then she should repeat the whole process for the other breast.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-524bae0d.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg">
Woman lies on pillow with right arm raised left hand palpates right breast with pads of fingers.
Woman lies on pillow with left arm raised above head, fingers of right hand squeeze nipple of left breast.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expression">Expression<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expression" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Finally, hold the nipples in between your fingers and express to check on unusual secretion, such as blood or pus.</p>
<p>The following are some warning signs to be noted upon examination:</p>
<ul>
<li>Unusual difference in size or shape of the breast</li>
<li>Alteration in the position of either nipple</li>
<li>Turning of colour of either nipple</li>
<li>Dimpling of the surface</li>
<li>Unusual rash on the breast or nipple</li>
<li>Unusual prominence of the veins over either breast or a discharge from the nipple</li>
<li>Unusual discrete lump or nodule on any part of either breast</li>
</ul>
<p>Should you find anything strange, report it to the doctor for further examination, investigation and management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pelvic-examination">Pelvic Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pelvic-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pelvic examination involves exploring the female pelvic organs using hands and speculum. The main objectives of pelvic examination are to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Detect pelvic abnormalities that may act as a limitation to a specific contraceptive technique, such as IUCD, and for diagnosis</li>
<li>Identify a pathological process that may have arisen incidental to, or as a complication of, any contraceptive</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Obtain specimen for laboratory studies such as cervical smear for papanicolau, culture for gonorrhoea, culture for sensitivity of any bacteria and/or wet vaginal smear</li>
<li>Determine uterine position, shape, size, consistency for IUCD insertion and vaginal condition for diaphragm fitting</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-4e23dac5.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<p>Aseptic technique has to be observed to ensure quality care is maintained and infection is prevented during the procedure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="items-required-for-a-pelvic-examination">Items Required for a Pelvic Examination:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#items-required-for-a-pelvic-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>One cusco speculum</li>
<li>One kidney dish</li>
<li>One galipot</li>
<li>Sterile cotton wool</li>
<li>Swab</li>
<li>Investigation form</li>
<li>Pairs of gloves</li>
<li>Sanitary pads</li>
<li>Scraping spatula</li>
<li>One sponge holding forceps</li>
<li>Antiseptic</li>
<li>Lubricant</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="speculum-examination">Speculum Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#speculum-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When conducting a speculum examination you should:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Explain the procedure to the patient</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Let the patient empty her bladder</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure privacy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Scrub your hands and put on gloves aseptically</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Put the patient in dorsal position on the couch and cover her up to the abdomen</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inspect external genitalia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lubricate the speculum with water</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Insert into the vagina with blades laterally</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Open blades and visualise the cervix then check for discharge, colour or erosion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Take specimen for laboratory test if indicated</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Unscrew and remove speculum, examine vaginal wall as you remove speculum</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bimanual-or-digital-examination">Bimanual or Digital Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bimanual-or-digital-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When conducting a digital examination you should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Swab the vulva with antiseptic systematically</li>
<li>Lubricate gloved fingers and insert into the vagina</li>
<li>Check the state of vagina as well as cystocele and rectocele</li>
<li>Locate the cervix, cervical OS whether anterior, midpoint or posterior</li>
<li>Check if position of uterus is anteverted or retroverted</li>
<li>Palpate adnexae for tenderness</li>
<li>Check pelvic muscle tone</li>
<li>As you come out squeeze Skene's glands</li>
<li>Check on your gloves. If there is blood, which indicates the patient is on menses, give pads</li>
<li>Make your patient comfortable</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="papanicolau-smear">Papanicolau Smear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#papanicolau-smear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is advisable for the patient to have a Papanicolau (Pap) smear yearly. A Pap smear consists of scrapings obtained from the cervix for cervical cytology. The purpose of the smear is to detect cancer of the cervix.</p>
<p>The following equipment is necessary to conduct the procedure:</p>
<ul>
<li>One cusco speculum</li>
<li>Two glass slides</li>
<li>One hard diamond pencil</li>
<li>One wooden spatula</li>
<li>One fixative solution</li>
<li>One pathological request form</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Swabs</li>
</ul>
<p>There are several points to remember when performing this procedure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="points-to-remember-when-performing-a-papanicolau-smear">Points to Remember When performing a Papanicolau Smear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#points-to-remember-when-performing-a-papanicolau-smear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Clean the slides and label correctly, using the diamond pencil, before taking smears.</li>
<li>Fill in the pathological form.</li>
<li>Speed is essential to prevent dying of cells.</li>
<li>Keep the slide with smear away from direct light.</li>
<li>Do not lubricate speculum with antiseptic. Tap water may be used.</li>
<li>Do not swab vulva with antiseptics.</li>
</ol>
<p>Now you have looked through the points to remember, you will look at how the procedure is performed.</p>
<p>Ensure privacy and explain the procedure to the patient. Let her empty the bladder. You should position her on a couch in the dorsal position with the abdomen covered. Insert speculum and after visualising the cervix, screw it into position. With the wooden spatula, scrape the cervical cells by rotating the end of the spatula through 360 in the cervical os.</p>
<p>Quickly spread the sample onto the slide and put a fixative solution or spray to fix it on the slide. Repeat the procedure for the second slide. Allow to dry and ensure that the specimen is taken to the laboratory immediately.</p>
<p>For further information refer to the Nursing Council Procedure Manual, pp. 278 - 279.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-the-pap-smear">Classification of the Pap Smear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-the-pap-smear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pap smear results are classified in the following manner:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Class I</th><th>Normal cells</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Class II</td><td>Minor infections, for example Moniliasis, Trichomonas</td></tr><tr><td>Class III</td><td>Suspicious of malignancy. In such case:  Repeat smear in three months  Refer for cone biopsy to confirm presence of cancer cells under a microscope</td></tr><tr><td>Class IV</td><td>A few cancer cells that can be treated successfully</td></tr><tr><td>Class V</td><td>Numerous malignant cells indicating definite cancer</td></tr><tr><td>---</td><td>---</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Both class IV and V should be referred to the Gynaecology Department urgently for appropriate treatment. (MOH:1988, NCK:1988, MOH:June 1997)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-2-natural-family-planning-nfp-and-lactation-amenorrhoea-lam">SECTION 2: NATURAL FAMILY PLANNING (NFP) AND LACTATION AMENORRHOEA (LAM)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-natural-family-planning-nfp-and-lactation-amenorrhoea-lam" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Natural family planning is an approach to the understanding and respecting of human sexuality with its inherent procreative capacity and its consequent responsibility. Any teaching of the natural methods of family planning is, therefore, within the context of strengthening the family bonds and promoting responsible parenthood and its pro-life.</p>
<p>The natural methods are based on simple observance of nature in regard to human fertility. The methods do not interfere with the body functions in any way. The natural family planning methods require the cooperation of both the husband and wife and the study and discussion of their combined fertility brings them closer together. The sacrifice and control they demand generate respect of love and life. Because this is a natural method it overcomes all barriers, such as religious, social or ethnic. NFP goes hand in hand with LAM. As the mother breastfeeds, ovulation is delayed for as long as two years thus reinforcing the relationship and baby care.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of the section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the three types of NFP</li>
<li>Describe how lactation amenorrhoea functions</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 221 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="natural-family-planning-fertility-awareness-based-method">Natural Family Planning (Fertility Awareness Based Method)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#natural-family-planning-fertility-awareness-based-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Natural Family Planning (NFP) is the oldest method of contraception. In our societies most tribes practiced some form of FP, such as when a mother was breast feeding it was a taboo to have sex as it was believed the baby would become sick and even die. The woman would abstain from sex for two to four years after childbirth. On some occasions she would even go back to her family home. Many communities also sanctioned polygamy, which allowed the man to have his sexual desires fulfilled while the mother was breast feeding.</p>
<p>As communities started changing, monogamy was embraced and the couple stayed in one house. As a result, new methods of FP came into existence to complement the NFP method.</p>
<p>Natural family planning refers to a way of life whereby a couple, if properly instructed, can choose to avoid or achieve pregnancy by applying the appropriate sexual behaviour during the fertile and infertile phases of the menstrual cycle without the use of chemicals or mechanical devices. NFP is also referred to as periodic abstinence, rhythm or fertility awareness method.</p>
<p>The NFP method seems to work best when couples are clear about whether they want to have a child or not. The method appeals to couples who feel that fertility control is a joint responsibility and that neither partner should be required to bear the brunt of the health burden.</p>
<p>NFP educates couples on their reproductive processes and human sexuality as they work in harmony to control or regulate their fertility. There are several methods of NFP.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="basal-body-temperature-bbt-method">Basal Body Temperature (BBT) Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basal-body-temperature-bbt-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a natural method of family planning and it involves the woman taking and recording her body temperature every morning before rising to know when ovulation occurs. In a healthy woman the body temperature remains relatively constant during the first phase of her menstrual cycle. Shortly before ovulation the temperature rises by about <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>0.2</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em"></mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.2^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">0.</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span> to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>0.5</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em"></mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.5^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">0.</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">5</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span> and stays elevated until the next menstrual period. The couple should avoid sexual intercourse during the period when BBT is high. They can have sex after the third day of consecutive high temperature until the beginning of next menstrual bleeding.</p>
<p>Note the following points when taking basal body temperature:</p>
<ul>
<li>It should be taken first thing in the morning before rising</li>
<li>Temperature should be recorded within same hour</li>
<li>Note temperatures taken outside the hour</li>
<li>Note all disturbances, for example, all medications</li>
<li>Use the same thermometer for the entire cycle</li>
<li>Note the use of a new thermometer</li>
<li>If the reading stops between two numbers ignore the high one and record the lower one</li>
</ul>
<p>In some circumstances the natural family planning method may fail due to individual physiological variations. To be more successful, a woman may have to use a combination of methods, referred to as 'sympto thermal' whereby the woman checks on the mucus as well as the temperature.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-sympto-thermal-method-which-combines-the-billings-and-basal-body-temperature-methods">The Sympto Thermal Method (which combines the Billings and Basal Body Temperature Methods)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-sympto-thermal-method-which-combines-the-billings-and-basal-body-temperature-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The sympto thermal method combines the recording of Basal Body Temperature (BBT) with observing the cervical mucus and other physical signs of ovulation. These physical signs include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Breast tenderness</li>
<li>Mid cycle pain</li>
<li>Spotting or bleeding</li>
<li>Abnormal heaviness</li>
<li>Cervical changes on position, degree of opening and texture, slippery and stretchy mucus</li>
</ul>
<p>The couple should abstain from sexual intercourse from the first appearance of the sensation of cervical mucus until after ovulation has been confirmed by three days of elevated temperature or four days of post ovulation mucus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="billings-ovulatory-method-bom-or-cervical-mucus-method">Billings Ovulatory Method (BOM) or Cervical Mucus Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#billings-ovulatory-method-bom-or-cervical-mucus-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This method is based on the ability to recognise fertile and infertile phases of the menstrual cycle. It requires a high level of motivation and cooperation from both partners. The woman needs to become aware of mucus changes and abstain from sexual intercourse to avoid pregnancy during the fertile period.</p>
<p>In the beginning, a daily record on the type of mucus is important until the patient becomes confident. This takes about one year. In order for you to understand and instruct patients to follow the Billings method you need to review the menstrual cycle.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-menstrual-cycle">The Menstrual Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-menstrual-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Failure of fertilisation results in menstruation. This discharge is shed from the endometrium. It consists not only of blood but also debris from the uterine wall in the form of mucus and fragments.</p>
<p>The menstrual cycle is defined as a series of physiological changes directly related to the development, regression and shedding of the endometrium under various hormonal influences.</p>
<p>The monthly cycle begins with the first day of bleeding and ends with the day before the next cycle begins. It varies in length but the average cycle is taken to be 28 days and reoccurs regularly from puberty to menopause, except when pregnancy intervenes.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-02ebbe62.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<p>There are three main phases and they affect the tissue structure of the endometrium controlled by ovarian hormones.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="can-you-list-the-three-phases-of-the-menstrual-cycle">Can you list the three phases of the menstrual cycle?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#can-you-list-the-three-phases-of-the-menstrual-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Did you remember the phases?</p>
<p>The three phases of the menstrual cycle are menses, proliferative and secretory. If you did not remember them, please go over module two unit two part one to refresh your memory.</p>
<p>You will now look at the phases step by step.</p>
<p>There are three main phases and they affect the tissue structure of the endometrium controlled by ovarian hormones.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="menstrual-phase">Menstrual Phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menstrual-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During the menstrual phase there is vaginal bleeding lasting three to five days. It is the terminal phase of the cycle when the endometrium is shed down to the basal layer along with blood from the capillaries and the unfertilised ovum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="proliferative-phase">Proliferative Phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#proliferative-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The proliferative phase follows menstruation and lasts up to ovulation. This phase is under the influence of oestrogen. There is growth and thickening of the endometrium in readiness to receive the fertilised ovum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="secretory-phase">Secretory Phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secretory-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the last stage and follows ovulation. It is also known as the luteal phase. It occurs under the influence of the progesterone hormone and oestrogen from corpus luteum. The endometrium</p>
<p>thickens and becomes spongy and the glands are more tortuous. If fertilisation does not occur, the ovum dies, the secretion of progesterone and oestrogen falls and the endometrium breaks, shedding blood as menstruation. (Bennett, et al: 1999)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-ec556ed4.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="changes-occurring-during-the-menstrual-cycle">Changes Occurring During the Menstrual Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#changes-occurring-during-the-menstrual-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should be aware of the following changes, which occur during the menstrual cycle:</p>
<ul>
<li>The human gonadotrophic hormone stimulates the ovaries to produce oestrogen and progesterone. At the same time, several ova begin to grow.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>As the ova are growing, the Graafian follicle surrounding the ova begins to produce high levels of oestrogen. Oestrogen causes several changes to occur during the fertile period.</li>
<li>Cervical mucus becomes profuse, slippery, stretchy and wet, raw egg white or clear and lubricative.</li>
<li>The vaginal secretions are also wet.</li>
<li>The cervix rises, softens, and opens to help the sperm travel into the uterus.</li>
<li>The basal body temperature is low.</li>
<li>The uterine lining increases in thickness and blood supply.</li>
</ul>
<p>The mucus performs several functions. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Protecting the sperm cells so that they retain their fertilising capacity for three days</li>
<li>Nourishing the sperm</li>
<li>May make the sperm cells capable of fertilisation</li>
<li>Filtering and destroying damaged sperm cells</li>
<li>Helping in sperm mobility as it forms guiding channels which help the sperm to move along the vagina through the cervix, uterus and into the fallopian tubes</li>
</ul>
<p>Ovulation occurs on the 14th day before the beginning of the next period. Once the ovum is released, it can only be fertilised within 24 hours. After ovulation, the hormone progesterone is produced and it enhances changes in the female reproductive system.</p>
<p>The infertile period is characterised by the following changes:</p>
<ul>
<li>The cervical mucus loses its quality (it feels dry and is no longer slippery and stretchy). It becomes milky, sticky, scanty, and thick and hinders sperm penetration into the uterus.</li>
<li>The cervix lowers down and becomes firm and closes passage for sperm to the uterus.</li>
<li>The basal temperature rises and remains the same for the rest of the cycle.</li>
</ul>
<p>If there is no fertilisation, the levels of oestrogen and progesterone fall and menstruation occurs around 12 to 14 days after ovulation.</p>
<p>The Billings method of contraception is applicable to all phases of a woman's reproductive life whether her menstrual cycles are regular or irregular, during adolescence,</p>
<p>when she is coming off the pill, when she is breast feeding, or approaching the menopause. (CDC: 1999, Hatcher et al: 1997)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mechanism-of-action-for-the-fertility-awareness-method">Mechanism of Action for the Fertility Awareness Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action-for-the-fertility-awareness-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method is based on the awareness of two major facts:</p>
<ul>
<li>A man's sperm can live in a woman's reproductive tract for three days.</li>
<li>The woman's ovum can be fertilised on the day of ovulation and a day after.</li>
</ul>
<p>This calls for the couple to be able to estimate at least four to five days in advance when the woman will ovulate. If they can identify when ovulation has occurred, they can then adjust their sexual practices depending on whether they want a pregnancy or not.</p>
<p>There are both advantages and disadvantages to NFP.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages">Advantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The disadvantages of this method include:</p>
<ul>
<li>For the cervical mucus and sympto thermal methods to be used correctly, the couple requires at least three cycles to be confident. This necessitates constant contact with the instructor.</li>
<li>Both partners have to be committed, motivated and cooperative for success. Where abstinence is required, male participation has been wanting.</li>
<li>It is less effective due to user errors.</li>
<li>It can cause emotional stress when the couple have to abstain for several days.</li>
<li>It does not protect against STI/HIV/AIDS.</li>
<li>It requires systematic charting.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>Despite the disadvantages, this method is very effective so long as the couple are cooperative and understand their responsibilities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lactational-amenorrhoea-lam-in-family-planning">Lactational Amenorrhoea (LAM) in Family Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lactational-amenorrhoea-lam-in-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Lactational Amenorrhoea is a family planning method based on the physiology of breast feeding. LAM involves the use of breast feeding as a temporary family planning method.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Breast feeding has the effect of stopping ovulation because it changes the rate of natural hormones for at least six months or longer. The mother is encouraged to start another method at the proper time. LAM has several advantages, which range from contraceptive to non-contraceptive.</p>
<p>Contraceptive advantages:</p>
<ul>
<li>Protection against pregnancy as long as full breast feeding is practised</li>
<li>No interference with sexual activity</li>
</ul>
<p>Non-contraceptive advantages:</p>
<ul>
<li>It can be used immediately after birth</li>
<li>No cost or supplies needed</li>
<li>It contributes to passive immunity for the child</li>
<li>It decreases exposure to pathogens in water and other milk</li>
<li>It incorporates the best source of nutrition to infants</li>
</ul>
<p>However, LAM does have one major limitation in that it is effective only when the mother is breast feeding for at least six months.</p>
<p>The LAM method is most suitable for mothers with babies less than six months of age and who are still amenorrhoeic. In addition:</p>
<ul>
<li>The baby is fully breast feeding, that is, 85% of feed is breast milk</li>
<li>The mother breast feeds often, both day and night</li>
<li>Baby feeds on demand</li>
<li>The mother's menstrual periods have not resumed</li>
<li>Baby not more than six months old</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember:
Pregnancy is possible with this method, so mothers should look for other effective methods as soon as possible.</p>
<p>SECTION 3: HORMONAL CONTRACEPTIVES</p>
<p>Introduction</p>
<p>In this section you will focus on synthetic hormonal contraceptives, which are like the natural hormones. When used effectively, these will hinder pregnancy.</p>
<p>Introduction</p>
<p>In this section you will focus on synthetic hormonal contraceptives, which are like the natural hormones. When used effectively, these will hinder pregnancy.</p>
<p>Hormonal Contraceptives</p>
<p>Can you think of four types of hormonal contraceptives you have seen in your health facility?</p>
<p>Have you listed:</p>
<ul>
<li>Combined oral contraceptives</li>
<li>Injectables</li>
<li>Implant</li>
<li>Progestin only pills</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now continue to cover each of them in greater detail.</p>
<p>Combined Oral Contraceptives (COCs)</p>
<p>Combined Oral Contraceptives (COCs) are made up of a combination of synthetic oestrogen and progesterone. The monophasic, which include microgynon, neogynon, eugynon and nordette, have a high level of oestrogen. Triphasics, including logynon and trinordial, have low oestrogen content and are preferred for teenagers and women over 35 years and those with acne.</p>
<p>COCs act in the following manner:</p>
<ul>
<li>Slow down the motility of the fallopian tubes delaying implantation</li>
<li>Delay or inhibit ovulation as the Follicle Stimulation Hormone (FSH) production is suppressed, which inhibits maturation of ovarian follicles</li>
<li>Mucus is too thick to be penetrated by the sperm</li>
<li>Endometrium is not well prepared for fertilised ovum due to low oestrogen levels</li>
</ul>
<p>The Advantages and Disadvantages of Combined Oral Contraceptives</p>
<p>There are several advantages and benefits associated with the use of combined oral contraceptives.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 225 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advantages-and-benefits-of-cocs">Advantages and Benefits of COCs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-and-benefits-of-cocs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>They are highly effective when used correctly</li>
<li>They are easy to use</li>
