<li>They are effective immediately</li>
<li>Non-clinical staff can provide them</li>
<li>A pelvic examination is not required to initiate use</li>
</ul>
<p>There are also non-contraceptive benefits, which include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Reduced menstrual flow, which reduces the risk of anaemia</li>
<li>Decreased dysmenorrhoea</li>
<li>Protection against benign cancers of the breast, ovary and endometrium</li>
<li>Prevention of ectopic pregnancy</li>
</ul>
<p>However, there are also several limitations, which should be taken into consideration.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="limitations-of-cocs">Limitations of COCs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#limitations-of-cocs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The effect is lowered by other drugs, such as anti-tuberculosis and anti-epileptic drugs</li>
<li>There can be serious side effects though these are rare (for example, stroke, myocardial infarction, venous thrombosis and adenomas)</li>
<li>They offer no protection against STIs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="who-can-use-combined-oral-contraceptives">Who Can Use Combined Oral Contraceptives?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-can-use-combined-oral-contraceptives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Combined oral contraceptives can be used by various categories of people.</p>
<p>COCs can be used by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sexually active women of reproductive age</li>
<li>Women with established menses</li>
<li>Women of any parity, nulliparous included</li>
<li>Breast feeding mothers after six months post natal, whose LAM criteria applies</li>
<li>Women who can follow a daily routine of pill taking</li>
<li>Women with anaemia</li>
<li>Women with severe dysmenorrhoea</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="who-should-not-use-combined-oral-contraception">Who should not use combined oral contraception?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-should-not-use-combined-oral-contraception" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are some women who are advised not to use combined oral contraceptives.</p>
<p>Women not advised to use COCs include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Breast feeding mothers before six months post partum</li>
<li>Women who are pregnant or suspect they are pregnant</li>
<li>Women with unexplained abnormal vaginal bleeding</li>
<li>Women with a history of blood clotting disorders</li>
<li>Women with a history of heart disease</li>
<li>Women with active liver disease</li>
<li>Women who are hypertensive with BP of 160/100 or over</li>
<li>Women with diabetes mellitus complicated by vascular disease</li>
<li>Women who smoke and are over 35 years</li>
<li>Women with sickle cell</li>
</ul>
<p>When recommending pills to a patient you should make sure that you give them the following instructions and that they fully understand.</p>
<ul>
<li>Pills should be taken at about the same time each day preferably at night after meals.</li>
<li>If one pill is missed it should be taken as soon as it is remembered, even if it means taking two pills the next day.</li>
<li>If the patient has missed two or more pills in any seven day period she should take the pill at once and continue as usual. However, she should also use condoms or spermicide, or avoid sex for seven days.</li>
<li>If on a 21 day packet pill, the patient should rest for seven days on completion of a packet, then start the next packet on day eight and continue throughout. If on 28 day packet, the pill should be taken continuously.</li>
<li>The patient should come to the clinic for a follow up, an annual check up and pap smear.</li>
</ul>
<p>You should always be on the look out for the following danger signs/serious side effects which need urgent medical attention:</p>
<ul>
<li>Abdominal pain</li>
<li>Chest pain and breathlessness</li>
<li>Headaches frontal in nature</li>
<li>Eye disturbance such as blurring or flashes</li>
<li>Severe calf muscle pain</li>
</ul>
<p>The above mentioned develop suddenly and are severe in nature. The patient should be advised</p>
<p>to stop taking the pills, use a back up method of contraception and consult the doctor or visit a clinic immediately.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="progestin-only-pills-pops">Progestin Only Pills (POPs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#progestin-only-pills-pops" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>POPs are pills that contain low doses of synthetic progestin. They work in the following manner:</p>
<ul>
<li>The cervical mucus is thickened, which impairs penetration by spermatozoa</li>
<li>POPs inhibits ovulation</li>
<li>POPs regress endometrium</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="can-you-think-of-three-types-of-pops-which-are-available-at-service-delivery-points">Can you think of three types of POPs which are available at service delivery points?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#can-you-think-of-three-types-of-pops-which-are-available-at-service-delivery-points" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Have you listed microlut, micronor and ovrette as the progestin only pills?</p>
<p>There are several contraceptive benefits of POPs. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Highly effective if correctly used</li>
<li>Immediate return to fertility on discontinuation</li>
<li>Pelvic examination is not required to initiate use</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition, there are also several non-contraceptive benefits, which should be taken into account, namely:</p>
<ul>
<li>Do not affect breast feeding</li>
<li>Lighter, shorter periods</li>
<li>Decrease in breast tenderness</li>
<li>Do not increase blood clotting</li>
<li>Decrease dysmenorrhoea</li>
<li>Protect against endometrial cancer</li>
</ul>
<p>The main limitations of POPs are that they provide a slightly lower level of contraceptive protection than combined oral pills. They also require strict pill taking, preferably at the same time every day. Effectiveness may be lowered by the use of other drugs, for example, anti-tuberculosis and anti-epileptic drugs. In addition, they do not provide any protection against STIs including Hepatitis B and HIV/AIDS.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-can-use-progestin-only-pills">Who Can Use Progestin Only Pills?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-can-use-progestin-only-pills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following categories of women are able to use progestin only pills:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Women of reproductive age</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Women of any parity, nulliparous included</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Breast feeding mothers after six weeks post partum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Heavy smokers of any age</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Women who can't use combined oral pills due to oestrogen related contra indications</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Post abortion patients</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Women with sickle cell disease, hypertension, and valvular heart disease</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>However, you should note that the following categories of women do not make ideal candidates for the use of progestin only pills:</p>
<ul>
<li>Breast feeding mothers who are less than six weeks post natal</li>
<li>Women who are pregnant or suspected to be pregnant</li>
<li>Women with unexplained abnormal vaginal bleeding</li>
<li>Women who have breast cancer or history of breast cancer</li>
<li>Women with active liver disease</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="emergency-hormonal-contraception-ec">Emergency Hormonal Contraception (EC)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-hormonal-contraception-ec" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Emergency contraception is most commonly used in cases of unplanned sex, rape or a burst condom. There are several types of emergency hormonal contraceptives:</p>
<ul>
<li>One tablet of 75 microgram pill (for example, postinor), which should be taken within 72 hours of unprotected intercourse. Repeat same dose within 12 hours. Requires total of two tablets of 75 micrograms pill.</li>
<li>Two tablets of 50 microgram pill (for example, eugynon), which should be taken within 72 hours of unprotected intercourse. Repeat the same dose in 12 hours. Requires total of four tablets of 50 microgram pill.</li>
<li>Four tablets of 30 microgram pill (for example, microgynon), which should be taken within 72 hours of unprotected intercourse. Repeat same dose in 12 hours. Requires total of eight tablets of 30 microgram pills.</li>
</ul>
<p>The main advantage of the emergency contraceptive is that it provides emergency protection for about 85% of those at risk. However, it has several limitations. It is only effective within 72 hours of unprotected intercourse. It cannot and should not be used as a regular method of contraception. It does not protect against STIs or HIV/AIDS. As a minimal side effect, it may cause nausea.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 226 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Remember:
Emergency contraception should be used by patients in need of emergency protection but should not be used by patients who require regular protection and/or patients who are known to be pregnant.</p>
<p>Injectables</p>
<p>There are several types of injectable contraception. These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Depo provera or megestron, which are given every three months (or 84 days) but can be given 28 days earlier or 14 days later.</li>
<li>Noristerat, which is given every two months (or 56 days) but can be given 14 days earlier or seven days later.</li>
<li>Monthly injectable, for example cyclofen, cycloprovera and norigynon. These are given every month but can be given up to three days earlier or later.</li>
</ul>
<p>The main contraceptive benefits are:</p>
<ul>
<li>They are highly effective and consistently inhibit ovulation.</li>
<li>A pelvic examination not required before starting.</li>
<li>They do not contain oestrogen so there are no risks of cardiac or blood clotting effects.</li>
<li>They are long acting methods.</li>
</ul>
<p>The major non-contraceptive benefits are:</p>
<ul>
<li>They protect against endometrial cancer.</li>
<li>They reduce menstrual flow.</li>
<li>They decrease sickle cell crises.</li>
<li>They help prevent ectopic pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<p>However, there are several limitations to this contraceptive method. There is the risk of a delay in fertility return for four or more months. There may be a change in the menstrual cycle. They do not protect against STIs, HIV/AIDS or Hepatitis B.</p>
<p>The following types of patients can use injectable contraceptives:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Women of reproductive age, including nulliparous, with established menses.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Those in need of high and longer protection.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Breast feeding mothers six weeks after delivery and immediately if not breast feeding or post abortion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Those with certain medical conditions including sickle cell, diabetes, and valvular heart disease. However, evaluation and medical follow up is required while on this method.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Those who cannot take a pill every day.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The following individuals should not use the injectable method of contraception. Women who:</p>
<ul>
<li>Are breast feeding before six weeks after delivery.</li>
<li>Are pregnant or suspect pregnancy.</li>
<li>Have active liver disease.</li>
<li>Indicate suspicious abnormal vaginal bleeding.</li>
<li>Have medical conditions, like ischaemic cardiovascular disease, diabetes mellitus with vascular disease or high blood pressure of 160/100 or more.</li>
</ul>
<p>Implants</p>
<p>An implant is also a progestin but is long acting. It is like a natural hormone made of six plastic capsules. One example is norplant 36mg, where each capsule consists of 6mg of levanogestrel. However, jadelle is currently the implant used in Kenya.</p>
<p>The main contraceptive benefits of the implant are:</p>
<ul>
<li>It is highly effective.</li>
<li>There is an immediate return to fertility.</li>
<li>It offers continuous long term protection (five years).</li>
</ul>
<p>The main non-contraceptive benefits of the implants are:</p>
<ul>
<li>No effect on breast feeding</li>
<li>Lighter, shorter periods</li>
<li>Decreased breast tenderness</li>
<li>Decreased dysmenorrhoea</li>
<li>Does not increase blood clotting disorder</li>
<li>Protects against endometrial cancer</li>
</ul>
<p>However, there are several limitations associated with the implant. It must be inserted and removed by trained providers. It involves minor surgery with appropriate infection prevention. You must practice asepsis on insertion and removal. Finally, it does not provide protection against STIs, HIV/AIDS or Hepatitis B.</p>
<p>Who Can Use Implants?</p>
<p>The following categories of women can use implants:</p>
<ul>
<li>Women of reproductive age</li>
<li>Women of any parity, nulliparous included</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Breast feeding mothers after six weeks post partum</li>
<li>Heavy smokers of any age</li>
<li>Women who cannot use combined oral pills due to oestrogen related contraindications</li>
<li>Post abortion patients</li>
<li>Women with sickle cell disease, hypertension or valvular heart disease</li>
</ul>
<p>However, there are several categories of women who cannot use implants and you must note these carefully:</p>
<ul>
<li>Breast feeding mothers less than six weeks post natal</li>
<li>Pregnant or suspected to be pregnant</li>
<li>Women with unexplained abnormal vaginal bleeding</li>
<li>Women who have breast cancer or history of breast cancer</li>
<li>Women with active liver disease</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-4-other-contraceptive-methods">SECTION 4: OTHER CONTRACEPTIVE METHODS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-4-other-contraceptive-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this last section on contraceptive technology you are going to cover Intra Uterine Contraceptive Devices (IUCDs), Voluntary Surgical Contraception (VSC) for instance Bilateral Tubal Ligation (BTL), and vasectomy. Lastly, you will cover the barrier (conventional) methods, which are condoms, spermicides, the vaginal sponge and diaphragm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe what is an intra uterine contraceptive device</li>
<li>Explain the two types of voluntary surgical contraception</li>
<li>List the common barrier methods used in FP</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="intrauterine-contraceptive-devices-iucds">Intrauterine Contraceptive Devices (IUCDs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intrauterine-contraceptive-devices-iucds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are plastic or medicated plastic objects designed in different shapes and forms which, when inserted into the uterine cavity, prevent pregnancy.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Spermatozoa immobility as the movement is hindered.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ovum motility increased in the fallopian tube so it reaches the uterus prematurely.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prostaglandin produced in the uterine cavity aids in expulsion of the zygote.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Implantation interfered with, as the IUCD occupies the space.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Endometrium: there is inflammatory process that is hostile for implantation.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>These are plastic or medicated plastic objects designed in different shapes and forms which, when inserted into the uterine cavity, prevent pregnancy.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>S</th><th>Spermatozoa immobility as the movement is hindered.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>O</td><td>Ovum motility increased in the fallopian tube so it reaches the uterus prematurely.</td></tr><tr><td>P</td><td>Prostaglandin produced in the uterine cavity aids in expulsion of the zygote.</td></tr><tr><td>I</td><td>Implantation interfered with, as the IUCD occupies the space.</td></tr><tr><td>E</td><td>Endometrium: there is inflammatory process that is hostile for implantation.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Can you list the different types of IUCD that you have heard of or know to be available in a health facility?</p>
<p>Did you think of these?</p>
<ul>
<li>Cu T 380A</li>
<li>Cu T 220</li>
<li>Nova T</li>
<li>Cu 7</li>
<li>Multi load 375</li>
<li>Multi load 250</li>
<li>Hormone releasing IUCDs eg mirena</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 228 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-53ef62a3.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"></p>
<p>There is also the Lippers loop, which is non-medicated and spiral shaped, with an indefinite life span. However, this is currently not in circulation. The medicated IUCD has a copper wire around the shaft that discharges copper ions which increases the efficiency.</p>
<p>The main contraceptive advantages of IUCDs are that they are highly and immediately effective,</p>
<p>offer long term protection before deciding on a permanent method and they enable an immediate</p>
<p>return to fertility upon termination of use.</p>
<p>IUCDs also have some non-contraceptive advantages, which include that there is no interference with intercourse. They can comfortably be used by breast feeding women.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="limitations-of-the-iucd">Limitations of the IUCD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#limitations-of-the-iucd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>On recommending IUCDs to the patient you should always ensure that they are aware of the following limitations:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The device requires a skilled and competent practitioner to insert it in order to prevent infection during insertion and removal.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It may increase menstrual flow and cramps for the first few months but the patient will eventually readjust.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The device does not prevent ectopic pregnancy.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It does not protect against STIs, HIV/AIDS and Hepatitis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The device may be expelled or translocated.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Perforation may occur if inserted by an unskilled provider.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-can-use-iucds">Who Can Use IUCDs?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-can-use-iucds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following categories of women can use IUCDs:</p>
<ul>
<li>Women of reproductive age irrespective of parity</li>
<li>Women and partners with low risk of STI</li>
<li>Breast feeding mothers</li>
<li>Post natal mothers, where a post partum IUCD is inserted from ten minutes to 48 hours post delivery</li>
</ul>
<p>Meanwhile certain women should not use IUCDs, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Women who have, or whose partners have, multiple sexual partners</li>
<li>Women who are pregnant or suspect pregnancy</li>
<li>Those with current, recent (within three months) or recurrent pelvic inflammatory disease</li>
<li>Women with anaemia</li>
<li>Women with unexplained abnormal vaginal bleeding</li>
<li>Women with cancer of the reproductive organs</li>
<li>Women with congenital uterine abnormalities or fibroids, which distort the uterine cavity</li>
<li>Recent septic abortion (in the past three months)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="can-you-think-of-five-instructions-you-would-give-a-woman-who-has-had-an-iucd-inserted">Can you think of five instructions you would give a woman who has had an IUCD inserted?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#can-you-think-of-five-instructions-you-would-give-a-woman-who-has-had-an-iucd-inserted" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Did you include the following?</p>
<ul>
<li>She should observe good personal hygiene to prevent infection.</li>
<li>She may have increased cramps and bleeding for the first three months. Advise her to use analgesics if pain is severe but reassure her that she will adjust with time. Ask her to come to the clinic if pain and bleeding are excessive.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 229 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>During menses, check pads before throwing them away to confirm the device has not been expelled.</li>
<li>Check on IUCD threads once every month after menses while bathing.</li>
<li>The IUCD failure rate is 1%.</li>
<li>The first review will be at six months, then yearly when general physical examination and Pap smear are done.</li>
</ul>
<p>You should also inform the patient that she should be aware of certain danger signs, which should be reported to the clinic. These include pelvic pain or painful intercourse, which means the IUCD could be dislodged. Any unusual bleeding or bad vaginal discharge could be indications of an infection. A missed period or other signs of pregnancy and missing IUCD strings should also be reported.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pelvic-examination-and-iucd-insertion-procedure">Pelvic Examination and IUCD Insertion Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pelvic-examination-and-iucd-insertion-procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The aseptic technique is observed. The following equipment should be used:</p>
<ul>
<li>Two cusco speculums</li>
<li>One tenaculum</li>
<li>One sponge holding forceps</li>
<li>One uterine sound</li>
<li>One curved pair of scissors</li>
<li>IUCD packet</li>
<li>Artery forceps</li>
<li>Non-toothed dissecting forceps</li>
<li>Kidney dishes</li>
<li>Suitable bowls for swabs</li>
<li>Sterile gloves</li>
<li>Sterile swabs</li>
<li>Sanitary pads (towels)</li>
<li>Antiseptic</li>
<li>Good lighting</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-2459fd25.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="speculum-examination">Speculum Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#speculum-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following procedure should be followed when conducting a speculum examination:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the procedure to the patient</li>
<li>Let the patient empty her bladder</li>
<li>Ensure privacy</li>
<li>Put the patient in the dorsal position and cover up the abdomen</li>
<li>Inspect the external genitalia</li>
<li>Lubricate the speculum with water</li>
<li>Insert the speculum into the vagina with blades laterally</li>
<li>Open the blades and visualise the cervix then check for discharge, colour and erosion</li>
<li>Take specimen for laboratory test if indicated</li>
<li>Unscrew and remove the speculum and examine the vaginal wall as you come out</li>
<li>After the speculum, you can then perform digital examination</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bimanual-or-digital-examination">Bimanual or Digital Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bimanual-or-digital-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following procedures should be followed when carrying out a bimanual examination:</p>
<ul>
<li>Swab the vulva with antiseptic systematically</li>
<li>Lubricate gloved fingers and insert into the vagina</li>
<li>Check the state of vagina</li>
<li>Locate the cervix, cervical os whether anterior, midpoint or posterior</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Check if the position of the uterus is anteverted or retroverted</li>
<li>Palpate the adnexae for tenderness</li>
<li>Check on the pelvic muscle tone</li>
<li>As you come out, squeeze Skene's glands</li>
<li>Check on the gloves for blood if on menses</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-there-is-any-possibility-of-pelvic-infection-or-pregnancy-do-not-insert-iucd">If there is any possibility of pelvic infection or pregnancy, do not insert IUCD.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-there-is-any-possibility-of-pelvic-infection-or-pregnancy-do-not-insert-iucd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iucd-insertion">IUCD Insertion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iucd-insertion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following procedure is to be adhered to when inserting the IUCD.</p>
<ul>
<li>After the bimanual examination, reinsert the second speculum</li>
<li>Screw after visualising the cervix</li>
<li>Swab the os with antiseptic using the sponge forceps x three</li>
<li>Apply tenaculum at 10 to 2 o'clock to position the uterus</li>
<li>Sound the uterus gently to get the measurements of uterine size</li>
<li>Load the IUCD while inside the pack and measure per uterine sound results, unpack then, without contamination, insert in situ gently as patient pants</li>
<li>Release wings by withdrawing the barrel, remove piston, position IUCD by pushing barrel up again (CUT 380A)</li>
<li>Withdraw barrel and shorten thread</li>
<li>Remove tenaculum</li>
<li>Clean cervix with antiseptic and arrest bleeding</li>
<li>Reinstruct patient and give return appointment</li>
<li>Decontaminate all the equipment used in the disinfectant using prevention of infection guidelines</li>
</ul>
<p>Review the instructions previously given with the patient after the IUCD insertion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iucd-removal">IUCD Removal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iucd-removal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The IUCD should be removed if the patient decides that they would like to change their contraceptive practices or if the device is causing undesirable effects.</p>
<p>The main requirements for IUCD removal are similar to the requirements for the pelvic examination in IUCD insertion, excluding:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Sponge holding forceps</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Artery forceps</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pair of scissors</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cusco speculum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Alligator forceps</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Antiseptic and sterile swabs</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The mother should be prepared physically and psychologically and placed in dorsal position. The procedure should then be conducted as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Perform digital and speculum examination</li>
<li>Clean the cervix and visualise the IUCD thread</li>
<li>Apply the tenaculum and align the uterus</li>
<li>Using the artery forceps, grasp the thread and apply traction as the mother pants</li>
<li>Show the device to mother on removal</li>
<li>Remove the tenaculum, clean cervix and arrest bleeding</li>
<li>Remove the speculum and make patient comfortable</li>
<li>Give a sanitary pad</li>
<li>Offer an alternative method of contraception if need be</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-09d544e9.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="voluntary-surgical-contraception">Voluntary Surgical Contraception<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#voluntary-surgical-contraception" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Voluntary Surgical Contraception (VSC) is a surgical means of permanently terminating fertility.</p>
<p>In the bilateral tubal ligation, both fallopian tubes are tied and cut to terminate the continuity pathway for spermatozoa and ovum.</p>
<p>In a vasectomy, both vas deferens are tied and cut so that spermatozoa do not reach the urethra to be deposited during intercourse. Thus the semen becomes sperm free.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bilateral-tubal-ligation">Bilateral Tubal Ligation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bilateral-tubal-ligation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The two methods of tubal ligation are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Laparatomy</li>
<li>Laparoscopy</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-3be53783.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<p>It is suitable for</p>
<ul>
<li>Those who have had their desired number of children</li>
<li>Those who have chronic medical conditions such as renal, heart, uterine and ovarian diseases</li>
<li>Those who want a permanent method of contraception (after counselling)</li>
<li>Those who understand and voluntarily follow an informed consent procedure after proper counselling</li>
</ul>
<p>Certain women are not advised to use this method of contraception.</p>
<p>Additionally, patients should be informed that there are certain limitations associated with the procedure.</p>
<p>Limitations associated with the procedure are:</p>
<ul>
<li>The procedure is generally irreversible and expensive</li>
<li>There are risks and side effects associated with anaesthesia</li>
<li>Risks related to surgical procedure such as bleeding, haematoma or infection</li>
<li>The method does not protect against STIs, HIV/AIDS</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vasectomy">Vasectomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vasectomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A vasectomy is recommended when the family has reached the desired family size, the wife has</p>
<p>contra indicated to surgical procedure and male participation is promoted.</p>
<p>However, you should note that the procedure is contra indicated in the following circumstances:</p>
<ul>
<li>A large hydrocele</li>
<li>Chronic genital tract infection</li>
<li>Diabetic patient</li>
<li>Inguinal hernia unless after repair</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-800ff4c1.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<p>The following instructions should be given to the patient following a vasectomy:</p>
<ul>
<li>Advise the patient to rest for two days and avoid heavy lifting for five to seven days.</li>
<li>A scrotal support should be used.</li>
<li>The vasectomy is not effective immediately. The semen has sperms for three to four months, therefore requiring ten to fifteen ejaculations to be free from semen.</li>
</ul>
<p>The barrier method can be used for protection meanwhile.</p>
<ul>
<li>Vasectomy has a failure rate of 0.3%</li>
</ul>
<p>The main complications of VSC are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Pain and bleeding which occurs due to surgery. Give analgesics for pain and watch for signs of bleeding and arrest it.</li>
<li>Infections mean a strict aseptic technique should be observed to prevent infection.</li>
<li>Granuloma/bleeders must be well ligated.</li>
<li>Medical legal social problems could occur if there is premature sexual intercourse before the semen is sperm</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 232 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>free. Counsel, reassure and give proper instruction to the patient.</p>
<ul>
<li>Anastomosis increases the failure rate.</li>
<li>The patient should be reassured with regard to sperm antibodies reaction.</li>
<li>The patient also needs reassurance, usually psychological about the possibility of impotence/low libido.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barrier-methods-of-contraception">Barrier Methods of Contraception<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barrier-methods-of-contraception" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The barrier methods are the last to be covered, not because they are a lesser method but because they may have to be used as a backup method for the prevention of STIs, HIV/AIDS while using those other methods.</p>
<p>The barrier method works by barring spermatozoa from getting into the cervix, uterus and fallopian tubes for fertilisation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="can-you-think-of-four-barrier-methods-most-commonly-used-in-family-planning">Can you think of four barrier methods most commonly used in family planning?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#can-you-think-of-four-barrier-methods-most-commonly-used-in-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Did you think of condoms, spermicide, diaphragm and vaginal sponge?</p>
<p>These methods will now be covered in more detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-condom">The Condom<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-condom" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a sheath that fits over the erect penis or is inserted into the vagina, and acts as a barrier to the transmission of semen into the vagina.</p>
<p>There are two types of condoms:</p>
<ul>
<li>Male condom</li>
<li>Female condom</li>
</ul>
<p>Condoms should be recommended in the following instances:</p>
<ul>
<li>For males who want to participate in family planning</li>
<li>As a temporary measure when not sure if patient is pregnant</li>
<li>For sexually active teenagers</li>
<li>For those patients contra indicated to other methods</li>
<li>To reduce the spread of STIs, HIV/AIDS</li>
</ul>
<p>You should always emphasise that there are certain problems associated with condom use, as follows.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The condom may slip. The male condom has to be properly applied and withdrawn when the penis is still erect.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It may tear. You should remove air.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The user may have an allergy to rubber.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is a failure rate of 2-15%.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It should be used only once and discarded.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Precautions should always be taken. Advise patients to check the expiry date and to ensure proper storage, use and disposal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diaphragm">Diaphragm<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diaphragm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a dome shaped rubber device with a flexible</p>
<p>rim inserted into the vagina prior to sexual intercourse</p>
<p>to prevent conception by forming a barrier. It has to</p>
<p>be removed six to eight hours after intercourse. Diaphragms are of different sizes so as to fit well the individual patient.</p>
<p>When using the diaphragm, the following precautions should be taken:</p>
<ul>
<li>Efficacy is improved if used with spermicides</li>
<li>The patient should ensure that it fits well</li>
<li>There is a failure rate of 2-15%</li>
</ul>
<p>Contra indications include an allergy to rubber, uterine prolapse and recurrent cystitis.</p>
<p>You should instruct the patient to remove the device six hours post intercourse and to ensure that it is washed and kept dry.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-f6bc1510.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vaginal-sponge">Vaginal Sponge<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaginal-sponge" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a synthetic sponge impregnated with spermicides, which is inserted high into the vagina. It is effective for up to 24 hours. People who have a vaginal infection or allergies should not use it. The device remains in situ for six hours after intercourse, after which it is removed and discarded.</p>
<p>The main disadvantage of the vaginal sponge is that it is very expensive.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spermicides">Spermicides<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spermicides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are usually supplied in the form of gels, aerosols, pessaries or foaming tablets, which are inserted high into the vagina.</p>

<li>They have a failure rate of 14-25%</li>

        // Theme toggle functionality
        const themeToggle = document.getElementById('theme-toggle');
        const html = document.documentElement;
        
        themeToggle.addEventListener('click', () => {
            const currentTheme = html.getAttribute('data-theme');
            const newTheme = currentTheme === 'light' ? 'dark' : 'light';
            
            html.setAttribute('data-theme', newTheme);
            localStorage.setItem('theme', newTheme);
        });
        
        // Load saved theme
        const savedTheme = localStorage.getItem('theme') || 'light';
        html.setAttribute('data-theme', savedTheme);
    </script>

# PDF to HTML Conversion System Prompt (v9.4.4) - Rich UI Edition

**Version:** 9.4.4  
**Last Updated:** December 25, 2025  
**Focus:** Modern UI/UX patterns with 100% content fidelity, nested lists, mathematical equations, and comprehensive interactive quiz system

---

## Overview

This is the comprehensive **PDF to HTML Conversion System Prompt - Rich UI Edition**, featuring enhanced content organization patterns, advanced UI components, mathematical equations support, interactive quiz system, and modern design systems while maintaining absolute content fidelity.

## Core Mission

Convert PDF documents into **visually stunning, accessible, and pedagogically effective** HTML pages while ensuring **100% VERBATIM content preservation**. Create highly appealing and effective learning materials with **modern UI/UX patterns**, that maintain absolute fidelity to the original text content with interactive quizzes to reinforce learning and assess comprehension.

---

##  CRITICAL: ANTI-SUMMARIZATION WARNING

###  ABSOLUTE PROHIBITION ON SUMMARIZATION

**This is the most important rule in this entire prompt:**

> **DO NOT SUMMARIZE, CONDENSE, SHORTEN, OR OMIT ANY CONTENT FROM THE SOURCE TEXT**

Every single paragraph, sentence, list item, heading, table row, callout, and detail from the source text MUST be transferred to the HTML output **verbatim** without exception.

### What This Means in Practice:

|  PROHIBITED |  REQUIRED |
|---------------|-------------|
| Combining multiple paragraphs into one | Keep every paragraph separate |
| Removing "redundant" or similar content | Include all content, even if repetitive |
| Shortening long explanations | Keep full explanations verbatim |
| Omitting examples or illustrations | Include all examples and illustrations |
| Merging list items | Keep every list item separate |
| Skipping introductory/transitional text | Include all introductory and transitional text |
| Simplifying technical language | Keep original wording exactly |
| Removing citations or references | Include all citations and references |
| Condensing tables | Keep complete tables with all rows |
| Excluding "minor" sections | Include ALL sections, regardless of size |

### Mandatory Verification Steps:

1. **Before submitting any HTML file**, run the detection script:
   ```bash
   python3 detect_summarization_simple.py topics/topic-XX.html content_cleaned.txt [start_line] [end_line]
   ```

2. **Acceptable thresholds**:
   - Word count ratio: ** 80%** (above this is acceptable)
   - Paragraph count ratio: ** 90%**
   - List item ratio: ** 85%**
   - H2 heading ratio: ** 90%**

3. **If any indicator shows "LOW" or "MISSING"**, the file is summarizing content and must be fixed.

4. **Common causes of summarization to avoid**:
   - Thinking certain content is "not important"
   - Combining similar paragraphs
   - Removing examples to "save space"
   - Shortening explanations for "brevity"
   - Skipping "obvious" or "well-known" content
   - Merging related concepts into single sections

### Remember:

> **The source text is the authority. If it's in the source, it must be in the HTML. No exceptions.**

---

## Image Handling & Lightbox

All images must be wrapped in a `content-figure` container with the `data-lightbox="true"` attribute to enable the click-to-zoom functionality.

### Image Source Reference

**IMPORTANT**: Use the **exact image filenames** as they appear in `content_cleaned.txt`. Do NOT rename or map images.

#### Image Usage Instructions
1. **Check `content_cleaned.txt`** for image references like:
   ```html
   <img src="assets/images/image-20251225-9d805e34.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg">
   ```
2. **Path Resolution Rule**: Use the correct relative path based on the HTML file's location:
   - **Files in `topics/` directory**: Use `../assets/images/`
   - **Files in root directory** (e.g., `index.html`, `comprehensive-exam.html`): Use `assets/images/`
3. **Do NOT rename** images from their timestamp format
4. **Do NOT use** numbered formats like `img-1.jpeg` - use the actual filename

### HTML Structure for Images

```html
<div class="content-figure" data-lightbox="true">
    <div class="figure-image-wrapper">
        <img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-9d805e34.jpeg" alt="[Alt Text]" class="figure-image">
        <div class="figure-overlay">
            <span class="overlay-icon"></span>
            <span class="overlay-text">Click to zoom</span>
        </div>
    </div>
    <p class="figure-caption">Fig. [X.Y]: [Caption Text]</p>
</div>
```

### Image Path Examples

```html
<!-- Correct: Use exact filenames from content_cleaned.txt -->
<img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-9d805e34.jpeg" alt="Gingivitis showing inflamed gums">
<img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-b2c235cf.jpeg" alt="Fibre-optic Endoscope">
<img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-f38697c2.jpeg" alt="Periodontitis diagram">

<!-- Incorrect: Don't use simplified numbered format -->
<img src="../assets/images/img-1.jpeg" alt="...">
<img src="../assets/images/img-12.jpeg" alt="...">
```

---

## Interactive Quiz System

### Quiz System Overview

The quiz system provides 8 different question types to assess learner comprehension. Quizzes are stored in JSON format with versioning support, rendered dynamically via JavaScript, and fully integrated with the existing Rich UI design system.

### Quiz Question Types

#### 1. Multiple Choice (Single Answer)
Standard single-answer questions with 2-6 options.
- **Use Case**: Testing recall of specific facts, definitions, concepts
- **Features**: Radio button selection, immediate feedback, explanation display

#### 2. Multiple Select (Multiple Correct Answers)
Questions where learners select all correct answers.
- **Use Case**: Testing comprehensive understanding of related concepts
- **Features**: Checkbox selection, partial credit option, "Select all that apply" indicator

#### 3. True/False
Binary choice questions for quick knowledge checks.
- **Use Case**: Verifying understanding of statements, common misconceptions
- **Features**: Two-option format, confidence indicator option

#### 4. Fill in the Blank
Text input questions with exact or fuzzy matching.
- **Use Case**: Testing terminology, formulas, key terms
- **Features**: Case-insensitive matching, multiple acceptable answers, hint system
- **CRITICAL**: Question text MUST include `__id__` placeholders (e.g., `__b1__`, `__b2__`) where input fields should appear
- **Example**: `"The liver converts ammonia into __b1__."` with blank ID `"b1"`

#### 5. Matching
Pair items from two columns (drag-and-drop or dropdown).
- **Use Case**: Testing relationships, associations, categorization
- **Features**: Drag-and-drop interface, dropdown fallback, visual feedback

#### 6. Ordering/Sequencing
Arrange items in correct order.
- **Use Case**: Testing processes, procedures, chronological events
- **Features**: Drag-and-drop reordering with live sorting, numbered positions, step validation
- **Implementation Note**: Use "live" sorting during `dragover` events for robust behavior across all environments (including local `file://` protocol).

#### 7. Short Answer
Free-text response with keyword matching.
- **Use Case**: Testing deeper understanding, explanations
- **Features**: Keyword detection, partial credit, model answer display

#### 8. Image-Based Questions
Questions involving image interaction (hotspots, labeling).
- **Use Case**: Anatomy, diagrams, visual identification
- **Features**: Clickable regions, label placement, image zoom

### Media Support (Optional)

Every question can optionally include media (image, video, audio, YouTube) and answer options can optionally include images. All media fields are **optional** - questions work perfectly with text only.

#### Supported Media Types
| Type | Description | Use Case |
|------|-------------|----------|
| `image` | Static image file | Diagrams, photos, charts |
| `video` | Video file (mp4, webm) | Demonstrations, procedures |
| `audio` | Audio file (mp3, wav) | Pronunciation, sounds |
| `youtube` | YouTube embed | Educational videos |

#### Image Answer Options
For multiple-choice and multiple-select questions, each option can optionally include an image. This is useful for visual identification questions where learners select from images rather than text.

####  CRITICAL: Quiz Media Path Resolution
Image and media paths in quiz data files MUST be relative to the **HTML file** that will host the quiz.
- If the quiz is hosted in a file within `topics/` (e.g., `topics/topic-01.html`), use `../assets/images/`.
- If the quiz is hosted in a file in the **root** (e.g., `comprehensive-exam.html`), use `assets/images/`.

### Quiz JSON Schema (v1.0)

Store quiz data in `quizzes/` directory with the following structure:

```
project-name/
 quizzes/
    quiz-schema.json          # Schema definition
    topic-01-quiz.json        # Quiz for topic 01
    topic-02-quiz.json        # Quiz for topic 02
    ...
```

#### Complete Quiz JSON Schema

```json
{
  "$schema": "http://json-schema.org/draft-07/schema#",
  "title": "Quiz Schema v1.0",
  "type": "object",
  "required": ["schemaVersion", "quizId", "metadata", "questions"],
  "properties": {
    "schemaVersion": {
      "type": "string",
      "description": "Schema version for compatibility",
      "pattern": "^\\d+\\.\\d+$",
      "example": "1.0"
    },
    "quizId": {
      "type": "string",
      "description": "Unique identifier for the quiz",
      "pattern": "^[a-z0-9-]+$"
    },
    "metadata": {
      "type": "object",
      "required": ["title", "topicId", "createdAt"],
      "properties": {
        "title": { "type": "string" },
        "description": { "type": "string" },
        "topicId": { "type": "string" },
        "difficulty": { "enum": ["beginner", "intermediate", "advanced"] },
        "estimatedTime": { "type": "integer", "description": "Minutes" },
        "passingScore": { "type": "integer", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 100 },
        "createdAt": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
        "updatedAt": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
        "tags": { "type": "array", "items": { "type": "string" } }
      }
    },
    "settings": {
      "type": "object",
      "properties": {
        "shuffleQuestions": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
        "shuffleOptions": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
        "showFeedback": { "enum": ["immediate", "end", "never"], "default": "immediate" },
        "allowRetry": { "type": "boolean", "default": true },
        "showCorrectAnswers": { "type": "boolean", "default": true },
        "timeLimit": { "type": "integer", "description": "Seconds, 0 for unlimited" }
      }
    },
    "questions": {
      "type": "array",
      "items": { "$ref": "#/definitions/question" }
    }
  }
}
```

#### Question Type Definitions

```json
{
  "definitions": {
    "question": {
      "type": "object",
      "required": ["id", "type", "question", "points"],
      "properties": {
        "id": { "type": "string" },
        "type": {
          "enum": [
            "multiple-choice",
            "multiple-select",
            "true-false",
            "fill-blank",
            "matching",
            "ordering",
            "short-answer",
            "image-based"
          ]
        },
        "question": { "type": "string" },
        "points": { "type": "integer", "minimum": 1 },
        "hint": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: Hint for the question" },
        "explanation": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: Explanation shown after answering" },
        "media": {
          "type": "object",
          "description": "OPTIONAL: Media attachment for the question",
          "properties": {
            "type": { "enum": ["image", "video", "audio", "youtube"] },
            "url": { "type": "string", "description": "URL to media file" },
            "alt": { "type": "string", "description": "Alt text for accessibility" },
            "caption": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: Caption below media" },
            "mimeType": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: MIME type for video/audio" },
            "videoId": { "type": "string", "description": "YouTube video ID (for youtube type)" },
            "startTime": { "type": "integer", "description": "OPTIONAL: Start time in seconds (youtube)" },
            "autoplay": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
            "loop": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
            "muted": { "type": "boolean", "default": false }
          }
        }
      },
      "allOf": [
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "multiple-choice" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "options": {
                "type": "array",
                "minItems": 2,
                "maxItems": 6,
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "required": ["id", "isCorrect"],
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string", "description": "Text label (OPTIONAL if image provided)" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" },
                    "image": {
                      "type": "object",
                      "description": "OPTIONAL: Image for this option",
                      "properties": {
                        "url": { "type": "string" },
                        "alt": { "type": "string" }
                      }
                    }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "multiple-select" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "options": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "required": ["id", "isCorrect"],
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string", "description": "Text label (OPTIONAL if image provided)" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" },
                    "image": {
                      "type": "object",
                      "description": "OPTIONAL: Image for this option",
                      "properties": {
                        "url": { "type": "string" },
                        "alt": { "type": "string" }
                      }
                    }
                  }
                }
              },
              "partialCredit": { "type": "boolean", "default": true }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "true-false" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "correctAnswer": { "type": "boolean" }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "fill-blank" } } },
          "then": {
            "description": " CRITICAL: The 'question' field MUST contain __id__ placeholders (e.g., __b1__, __b2__) that match the blank IDs. Example: 'The liver converts ammonia into __b1__.' with blank id='b1'",
            "properties": {
              "blanks": {
                "type": "array",
                "description": "Array of blank definitions. Each blank.id must have a matching __id__ placeholder in the question text.",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string", "description": "Blank identifier (e.g., 'b1', '1', 'answer1'). Must match placeholder in question." },
                    "acceptedAnswers": { "type": "array", "items": { "type": "string" }, "description": "List of acceptable answers" },
                    "caseSensitive": { "type": "boolean", "default": false }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "matching" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "pairs": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "left": { "type": "string" },
                    "right": { "type": "string" }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "ordering" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "items": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string" },
                    "correctPosition": { "type": "integer" }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "short-answer" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "keywords": { "type": "array", "items": { "type": "string" } },
              "minKeywords": { "type": "integer" },
              "modelAnswer": { "type": "string" },
              "maxLength": { "type": "integer" }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "image-based" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "imageUrl": { "type": "string" },
              "imageAlt": { "type": "string" },
              "hotspots": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "x": { "type": "number" },
                    "y": { "type": "number" },
                    "radius": { "type": "number" },
                    "label": { "type": "string" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" }
                  }
                }
              },
              "options": {
                "type": "array",
                "description": "OPTIONAL: Alternative to hotspots for multiple-choice style image questions",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "required": ["id", "isCorrect"],
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        }
      ]
    }
  }
}
```

{

#### Example 5: Fill-Blank Question - Correct vs Incorrect Usage

** CRITICAL REQUIREMENT**: The question text MUST include `__id__` placeholders that match the blank IDs.

#####  CORRECT - Single Blank

```json
{
  "id": "q1",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The accumulation of serous fluid in the peritoneal cavity seen in cirrhosis is called __b1__.",
  "points": 10,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["ascites"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ],
  "explanation": "Ascites is the accumulation of fluid in the peritoneal cavity."
}
```

#####  CORRECT - Multiple Blanks

```json
{
  "id": "q2",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The liver converts ammonia into __b1__, which is then excreted by the __b2__.",
  "points": 15,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["urea"], "caseSensitive": false },
    { "id": "b2", "acceptedAnswers": ["kidneys", "kidney"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ],
  "explanation": "Ammonia is converted to urea by the liver and excreted by the kidneys."
}
```

#####  CORRECT - Numeric IDs

```json
{
  "id": "q3",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The heart has __1__ chambers: two __2__ and two __3__.",
  "points": 15,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "1", "acceptedAnswers": ["four", "4"], "caseSensitive": false },
    { "id": "2", "acceptedAnswers": ["atria", "atriums"], "caseSensitive": false },
    { "id": "3", "acceptedAnswers": ["ventricles"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ]
}
```

#####  INCORRECT - Missing Placeholder

```json
{
  "id": "q_wrong",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The accumulation of serous fluid in the peritoneal cavity is called _______.",
  "points": 10,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["ascites"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ]
}
```
**Problem**: Uses `_______` instead of `__b1__`. The quiz engine won't render an input field!

#####  INCORRECT - Mismatched IDs

```json
{
  "id": "q_wrong2",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The liver converts ammonia into __answer__.",
  "points": 10,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["urea"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ]
}
```
**Problem**: Question uses `__answer__` but blank ID is `b1`. They must match exactly!

##### Key Rules for Fill-Blank Questions:
1. **Placeholder Format**: Use double underscores: `__id__` (not single `_id_` or dashes `---`)
2. **ID Matching**: Placeholder `__b1__` must match blank `"id": "b1"` exactly
3. **Multiple Blanks**: Each blank needs its own unique ID and placeholder
4. **Accepted Answers**: Provide multiple acceptable variations (e.g., `["urea", "Urea"]`)
5. **Case Sensitivity**: Set `caseSensitive: false` for most medical terminology



### Quiz Loading Methods

The quiz system supports 3 loading methods (tried in order):

| Method | Attribute | Works with file:// | Requires Server |
|--------|-----------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **JSONP (Recommended)** | `data-quiz-js` |  Yes | No |
| Fetch API | `data-quiz-src` |  No | Yes |
| Embedded JSON | `<script id="quiz-data-[id]">` |  Yes | No |

#### Method 1: JSONP Script Loading (Recommended)

**Best for:** Opening HTML files directly in browser (`file://` protocol)

Create quiz as a `.js` file that calls `registerQuiz()`:

```javascript
// quizzes/topic-01-quiz.js
registerQuiz("topic-01-quiz", {
  "schemaVersion": "1.0",
  "quizId": "topic-01-quiz",
  "metadata": { ... },
  "questions": [ ... ]
});
```

HTML usage:
```html
<div class="quiz-container" 
     data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz"
     data-quiz-js="../quizzes/topic-01-quiz.js">
```

#### Method 2: Fetch API (Requires Web Server)

**Best for:** Deployment on web servers (http/https)

```html
<div class="quiz-container" 
     data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz"
     data-quiz-src="../quizzes/topic-01-quiz.json">
```

#### Method 3: Embedded JSON

**Best for:** Single-file distribution

```html
<script type="application/json" id="quiz-data-topic-01-quiz">
{
  "schemaVersion": "1.0",
  "quizId": "topic-01-quiz",
  ...
}
</script>

<div class="quiz-container" data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz">
```

### Quiz HTML Integration

Add quiz sections to topic pages using this structure:

```html
<!-- Quiz Section -->
<section class="quiz-section" id="topic-quiz" aria-labelledby="quiz-title">
    <div class="quiz-header">
        <div class="quiz-badge">
            <span class="quiz-icon"></span>
            <span>Knowledge Check</span>
        </div>
        <h2 id="quiz-title" class="quiz-title">Test Your Understanding</h2>
        <p class="quiz-description">Complete this quiz to assess your comprehension of the topic.</p>
    </div>
    
    <!-- Quiz Container - JSONP method (works with file://) -->
    <div class="quiz-container" 
         data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz"
         data-quiz-js="../quizzes/topic-01-quiz.js">
        
        <!-- Loading State -->
        <div class="quiz-loading">
            <div class="quiz-spinner"></div>
            <p>Loading quiz...</p>
        </div>
        
        <!-- Quiz Content (injected by JS) -->
        <div class="quiz-content" hidden></div>
        
        <!-- Quiz Results (shown after completion) -->
        <div class="quiz-results" hidden></div>
    </div>
</section>
```

<!-- In the <head> or before closing </body> -->
